## k9ew
“its top was above the branches of the other trees.” Some versions of the Bible translate this as “the top of the tree was in the clouds.”

# 31:11
## px3j
The word “hand” represents control. Alternate translation: “I put it in the power of the strongest nation” or “I gave the strongest nation power over it” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## xdq6
“I sent the cedar away from the cedar’s land because the cedar was wicked”

# 31:12
## cj68
See [[EZK-cj68]]
## m12k
The abstract noun “terror” can be stated as “afraid.” And here “nations” represents the people of the nations. Alternate translation: “who made the people of all the nations afraid” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

## cu9y
“cut the cedar down”

Boughs are very large branches that grow on trees. Usually, many smaller branches grow on the boughs.

## uf9q

# 31:14
## gp3y
“that no other trees that get a lot of water”

# 31:15
## zty8
See [[EZK-zty8]]
## qq6r
The phrase “went down to Sheol” means “died.” Alternate translation: “On the day that the cedar died” or “On the day that the cedar was chopped down” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## ry34
The abstract noun “mourning” can be stated as a verb. Alternate translation: “I caused the earth to mourn” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## xaz6
The word “covered” possibly refers to putting on clothes for mourning. Alternate translation: “I made the water from the springs mourn for the cedar” or “it was as though the springs that watered it mourned for it” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

“I kept the water in the ocean from watering the earth”

## j8ug

# 31:16
## i54z
See [[EZK-i54z]]
## i84r
Here “threw it down to Sheol” is an idiom that means to kill. “The pit” refers to the grave; because the grave was thought to be the entrance to the world of the dead, the pit also represents that world. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 31:14](../31/14.md). Alternate translation: “when I killed the cedar and it went to Sheol with everyone else that is dead” (See: [[figs-idiom]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

## cc1y
“that were already deep down in the ground.” This is an idiom. Alternate translation: “that had already died and are now in Sheol” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## fpl1
“the best trees of Lebanon that everyone would want; trees that got a lot of water.” This is describing the trees of Eden that were in the lowest parts of the earth.

## c1t9
This is something that everyone would want because it is very good.

# 31:17
## wir1
See [[EZK-wir1]]
## nmq8
Here “went down … to Sheol” is an idiom that means to die. Alternate translation: “those trees of Lebanon also died and went down to Sheol with the cedar” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## pk4t
Here “sword” represents enemies who fought them in battle. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “whom enemies had killed with swords” or “who had died in battle” (See: [[figs-activepassive]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

## j8k6
“These trees of Lebanon were its strong arm.” The phrase “strong arm” represents “power.” Alternate translation: “These trees of Lebanon were the power of the cedar” or “These trees strengthened the cedar” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 31:18
## uk5x
“Which of these trees in Eden had as much glory as you and was as great as you?” God asks Pharaoh this question to show him that the parable applies to him and his country. It can start with “So Pharaoh” or “So Egypt.” Alternate translation: “None of the trees in Eden was your equal in glory and greatness!” (See: [[figs-rquestion]])

## el53
This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “For I will bring you down” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## qmp4
“like the other trees of Eden”

“to a place deep in the ground”

## m128
“where you will be with people who are not circumcised”

Yahweh speaks of himself by name to express the certainty of what he is declaring. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 5:11](../05/11.md). Alternate translation: “this is what the Lord Yahweh has declared” or “this is what I, the Lord Yahweh, have declared” (See: [[figs-123person]])

# 32:intro
## vpr6

# 32:1
## r6qy
This phrase is used here to mark the beginning of a new part of the story. If your language has a way for doing this, you could consider using it here.

## esv2
This is the twelfth and final month of the Hebrew calendar. The first day is near the end of February. (See: [[translate-hebrewmonths]] and [[translate-ordinal]])

## vh9u
This refers to the twelfth year of the reign of King Jehoiachin. Alternate translation: “of the twelfth year of the exile of King Jehoiachin” (See: [[translate-ordinal]] and [[figs-explicit]])

## alb1
This is an idiom that is used to introduce something that God told his prophets or his people. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 3:16](../03/16.md). Alternate translation: “Yahweh spoke this message” or “Yahweh spoke these words” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 32:2
## l8pu
“Son of a human being” or “Son of humanity.” God calls Ezekiel this to emphasize that Ezekiel is only a human being. God is eternal and powerful, but humans are not. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 2:1](../02/01.md). Alternate translation: “Mortal person” or “Human”

## iu25
“sing”

## w2mp
Possible meanings are (1) he thought he was like a lion, but he was really only a monster, or (2) he was like a lion and a monster.

## u588
Egypt was stronger than other nations, like lions are stronger than other animals. (See: [[figs-simile]])

## v3jk
Pharaoh was powerful, but he only caused trouble for others, like this monster in the water. (See: [[figs-simile]])

## ih5d
A monster is an animal that is big and dangerous. This one might be a crocodile. See how you translated this word in [Ezekiel 29:3](../29/03.md).

# 32:3
## kkk6
See [[EZK-kkk6]]
## rvm9

# 32:4
## y8ig
“I will leave you helpless on the land.” The monster that was fearsome and powerful when it was in the water cannot do anything when it is left on dry land.

## hw9d
“all the birds that fly in the sky”

## vq12
This can be put into active form. Alternate translation: “I will let all the animals of the earth eat your body until they are hungry no longer” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 32:7
## p9yx
See [[EZK-p9yx]]
## fg4i
It was common to speak of a person’s life as if it were a lamp that could be put out. Alternate translation: “When I destroy you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## ih1k
Yahweh speaks of making the stars dark as if he were putting a cover over the sky. Alternate translation: “I will make everything in the sky go dark” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## q8bu

# 32:9
## tl12
See [[EZK-tl12]]
## t2sg
Here “heart” represents the people’s emotions. Alternate translation: “I will make the hearts of many peoples afraid” or “I will cause many people to be terrified” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## ss3w
The way that Yahweh destroys Egypt will make afraid even people in lands that Pharaoh never knew about.

## j9w1
The nation of Egypt, symbolized by its king, is spoken of as if it were a building that was collapsing. Alternate translation: “when nations hear about the way I destroyed you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 32:10
## nm9u
Here swinging a sword represents using the sword. Alternate translation: “when I use my sword” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## taf8
Here “tremble” is an action that people often do when they are very afraid. Alternate translation: “Every one of them will keep shaking because of their fear”

## j552
The idea of falling down (“downfall”) represents dying. Alternate translation: “when I destroy you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 32:11
## mza2
See [[EZK-mza2]]
## j9j7
Here “sword” represents an army. Alternate translation: “The army of the king of Babylon will attack you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 32:12
## l2us
The abstract noun “terror” can be stated as “terrifies” or “afraid.” Alternate translation: “Each warrior terrifies the nations” or “each one of them makes the nations afraid” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## lft6
The abstract noun “pride” can be stated as “proud.” Alternate translation: “will cause the Egyptians to no longer be proud” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## i7f7
Here “all” is probably a generalization that refers to the killing of large numbers of soldiers, and perhaps other people also. Alternate translation: “kill a very large number of people who live in Egypt” (See: [[figs-hyperbole]])

# 32:13
## h1tx
See [[EZK-h1tx]]
## n7m4
“in the places where there is a lot of water”

## cr7b

## lvt6
make clear water muddy

## d8xw
The hoof is a synecdoche for cattle. Alternate translation: “cattle stir them with their hooves” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 32:14
## siz7
Possible meanings are (1) “I will make the water calm” or (2) “I will make the water clear.” When no one stirs up the water, the dirt settles down and the water becomes clear.

## viv4

Here the idea of attacking represents destroying. Alternate translation: “when I destroy all who live in her” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## j4jw
It was normal in biblical language to represent countries and lands as if they were women. Alternate translation: “in it” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## jpw4
When Yahweh says that people will know that he is Yahweh, he is implying that they will know that he is the one true God who has supreme authority and power. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 6:7](../06/07.md). Alternate translation: “understand that I am Yahweh, the one true God” or “realize that I, Yahweh, have supreme power and authority” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

It was normal in biblical language to represent countries and lands as if they were women. Alternate translation: “over it” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## y6w8

## hbi3
This phrase is used here to mark the beginning of a new message. If your language has a way for doing this, you could consider using it here.

This is an idiom that is used to introduce something that God told his prophets or his people. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 3:16](../03/16.md). Alternate translation: “Yahweh spoke this message” or “Yahweh spoke these words” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 32:18
## l4kp
“Son of a human being” or “Son of humanity.” God calls Ezekiel this to emphasize that Ezekiel is only a human being. God is eternal and powerful, but humans are not. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 2:1](../02/01.md). Alternate translation: “Mortal person” or “Human”

## uqn6
God is perhaps telling Ezekiel to cause this to happen by giving a prophetic command.

## x2hj

## b9j9
“to the places under the ground.” When people died, they were put in the ground. So “bring them down … to the lowest earth” means “make them die.” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## map2

## rhr2

## fu9n

## b7dx

## a2ia
It is implied that they must go down to Sheol. Alternate translation: “Go down to Sheol” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## jc5b
as in death. If your language has a word for dead people lying down that is different from the word for live people lying down to sleep, use it here.

## t65u

# 32:20
## uu81
“Egypt and her people will fall”

## f6rm
The word “sword” is a metonym for a soldier who kills people with a sword.This can be put into active form. Alternate translation: “whom enemy soldiers killed with swords” or “who died in battle” (See: [[figs-activepassive]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

## lfy2
The word “sword” here is a metonym for war that people fight with swords. This can be translated in active form. Alternate translation: “War has begun” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

## d149
This can be put in active form. Alternate translation: “I have given Egypt to the sword” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## h27l
“about the Egyptians and those who join them”

# 32:22
## gvj6

## sx45

## db7h
“all her people together”

## sb68
The word “sword” is a metonym for soldiers who use swords to kill people. This can be put in active form. Alternate translation: “Soldiers used swords to kill them all” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

# 32:23
## g6yx
“The pit” refers to the grave; because the grave was thought to be the entrance to the world of the dead, the pit also represents that world. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 32:18](../32/18.md). (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## bp7y
This can be put in active form. Alternate translation: “all those whom enemies killed in battle” (See: [[figs-activepassive]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

# 33:1
## zsm8

# 33:2
## ncc7
“Son of a human being” or “Son of humanity.” God calls Ezekiel this to emphasize that Ezekiel is only a human being. God is eternal and powerful, but humans are not. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 2:1](../02/01.md). Alternate translation: “Mortal person” or “Human”

# 33:21
## f5bc
This phrase is used here to mark the beginning of a new part of the story. If your language has a way for doing this, you could consider using it here.

## ft4b
“year 12 … day 5 … month 10” (See: [[translate-ordinal]])

## h8in
This is the tenth month of the Hebrew calendar. The fifth day is near the beginning of January on Western calendars. (See: [[translate-hebrewmonths]] and [[translate-ordinal]])

## b544
Here “our” refers to Ezekiel and the Israelites who have been in Babylon since the time the Babylonians forced King Jehoiachin to leave Jerusalem, but not to the reader. Alternate translation: “after we became captives” or “after the Babylonians took us as captives to Babylon” (See: [[figs-exclusive]] and [[figs-explicit]])

## t9rx
“someone escaped from Jerusalem and came to me” The Babylonians had destroyed Jerusalem and killed the people of Jerusalem, but a few people escaped.

## v51g
The phrase “the city” refers to “Jerusalem.” This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “The Babylonians have destroyed Jerusalem” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

# 33:22
## q98f
The word “hand” is often used to refer to someone’s power or action. A person with his hand on another person has power over that person. See how you translated a similar phrase in [Ezekiel 1:3](../01/03.md). Alternate translation: “Yahweh was controlling me” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## hm5u
This phrase is an idiom that means to be able to speak. It can be stated in active form. See how you translated “I will open your mouth” in [Ezekiel 3:27](../03/27.md). Alternate translation: “I was able to speak” or “Yahweh enabled me to speak” (See: [[figs-idiom]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

## inm6
The word “dawn” refers to the time early in the morning when the light of the sun first appears.

## v9lp
“I was no longer forced to be silent” or “I was no longer unable to speak” Ezekiel had been unable to speak anything except prophetic words since [Ezekiel 3:26](../03/26.md).

## iv1s

## ej5p

“none of my shepherds tried to find my flock”

## zmc2
“shepherded themselves” or “fed and cared for themselves”

## cn7m
“did not feed and care for my flock”

# 34:9
## n7p3
See [[EZK-n7p3]]
## k6pi
“listen to Yahweh’s message.” This is an idiom that is used to introduce a special message from God. (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 34:10
## tc6r
This can be stated in the first person. Alternate translation: “I, the Lord Yahweh, say this” (See: [[figs-123person]])

## ygs2
The word “Behold” here adds emphasis to what follows. Alternate translation: “Indeed!”

## ejn3
“I am opposed to the shepherds”

## q2jt
The phrase “require … from their hand” is an idiom that means to hold or consider someone responsible for something. Alternate translation: “I will hold them responsible for all the bad things that happen to my flock” or “I will punish them for all the bad things they let happen to my flock” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

## wm3e
“I will not let them shepherd the flock any longer” or “I will not let them be the shepherds of the flock any longer”

## vs2t
“feed and take care of themselves”

## e7dg
Here “mouths” represent eating. Alternate translation: “so they cannot eat them” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## tzt6
“the shepherds will no longer eat the sheep and the goats of my flock”

# 34:11
## b4w4
See [[EZK-b4w4]]
## hn5p
This can be stated in first person. Alternate translation: “For this is what I, the Lord Yahweh, say” (See: [[figs-123person]])

## l3df
The word “Behold” here alerts the shepherds to pay attention to the surprising information that follows.

## i1zl
“will look for”

# 34:12
## gt3a
“with his scattered flock”

## hyn7
It is implied that the animals in the flock scattered because they did not have a shepherd to care for them or protect them. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “they scattered because they did not have a shepherd to care for them” (See: [[figs-explicit]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

## vtv8
“on the cloudy and dark day.” Disasters are spoken of as if they were a day of darkness. Alternate translation: “when terrible disasters happened to them” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 34:13
## n8pb
“bring my sheep and my goats” or “bring my flock”

## g4u8
“from the places where they lived with other peoples”

## j5tp
Yahweh bringing his people back from exile to their land so that he can care for them and keep them safe is spoken of as if he were their shepherd who puts his flock in a place where there is plenty of land, food, and water. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## hy5g
land that has grass and small plants that sheep and goats can eat

## z8xx
This is a place where people live. Usually they live in houses in a settlement.

## j7q2
“places where they can eat”

## i386
“lands that have a lot of grass and plants to eat”

## h7ir
eat grass and other plants

# 34:15
## zzp6
The word “myself” adds emphasis. God would do this because the shepherds were not doing it. (See: [[figs-rpronouns]])

## l72w
“will feed and take care of”

# 34:16
## u7yj
The words “the sheep or goats” are left out of this phrase, but they are intended to be understood. Alternate translation: “the sheep or goats that are lost” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

## xgj4
“bring back those that others have chased away”

## fzy3
“wrap a cloth around any sheep’s broken bone” or “wrap a cloth around any sheep’s wound”

## bi2r
The word “sheep” is understood. Alternate translation: “the fat sheep and the strong sheep” (See: [[figs-ellipsis]])

# 34:17
## y2f2

## ql1g
“pay attention, because what I am about to say is both true and important, I”

## j47n
“I will judge between one sheep and another”

## iya2
The male sheep and goats are usually the strongest in the flock and can get whatever they want from the other animals in the flock.

# 34:18
## fhe3
God uses these questions to scold Israel’s leaders, who are spoken of as if they were the stronger animals in the flock that were unkind to the weaker ones. You can translate this as a statement as in the UST. (See: [[figs-rquestion]] and [[figs-metaphor]])

## y9ed
“will make sure that the fat sheep and goats and the skinny sheep and goats are treating each other fairly”

## r517
The leaders and strong people in Israel are spoken of as if they were fat and strong animals in the flock. The poor and weak people in Israel are spoken of as if they were the thin and weak animals in the flock. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## e6ay
The word “you” refers to the sheep and goats that were not treating other sheep and goats well.

# 34:23
## imy5

## yh5c
The descendant of David who will be king over the people of Israel is spoken of as if he would be their shepherd. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## nw1h

## srq2

## gz6y
When Yahweh says that people will know that he is Yahweh, he is implying that they will know that he is the one true God who has supreme authority and power. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 6:7](../06/07.md). Alternate translation: “understand that I am Yahweh, the one true God” or “realize that I, Yahweh, have supreme power and authority” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## y578
Slavery is spoken of as if it were a yoke that people wear like some animals. Alternate translation: “when I free them from being slaves” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## c8kl

# 34:29
## w9v8
“be starved” or “be starving because of lack of food”

## g731

# 34:30
## s92f

## j3r4
This can be stated as one sentence. Alternate translation: “with them, and that they are my people”

# 35:intro
## nzj1
See [[EZK-nzj1]]
# 35:1
## e4ea
See [[EZK-e4ea]]
## ir7d
This is an idiom that is used to introduce something that God told his prophets or his people. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 3:16](../03/16.md). Alternate translation: “Yahweh spoke this message” or “Yahweh spoke these words” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 35:2
## dl8l
“Son of a human being” or “Son of humanity.” God calls Ezekiel this to emphasize that Ezekiel is only a human being. God is eternal and powerful, but humans are not. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 2:1](../02/01.md). Alternate translation: “Mortal person” or “Human”

## pzl8
Mount Seir was far away, so Ezekiel could not see it, but Yahweh commands him to stare in that direction as a symbol of harming the people there. See how you translated a similar phrase in [Ezekiel 6:2](../06/02.md). Alternate translation: “turn toward Mount Seir and stare” or “stare toward Mount Seir so that the people there will be harmed” (See: [[translate-symaction]])

## xr3k
“the mountain of Seir.” Yahweh tells Ezekiel to speak to Mount Seir as if it could hear him. The message is for all of the people of Edom. Alternate translation: “Mount Seir and prophesy against it because of what the people of Edom have done” (See: [[figs-personification]])

# 35:3
## c8g8
“to the mountain” or “to the people of Edom”

## mle2
Yahweh tells Ezekiel to speak to Mount Seir as if it could hear him. The message is for all of the people of Edom. Alternate translation: “Listen, Mount Seir, I will strike you with my hand and make you a desolation and a waste because of what your people did” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## dn2p
The word “Behold” here adds emphasis to what follows. Alternate translation: “Listen!” or “Indeed!”

## sjk1
“I am your enemy” or “I oppose you”

## a49m
Here “hand” represents power. Alternate translation: “I will use my power to strike you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## s7v8
The abstract noun “desolation” can be translated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “make you desolate” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## yv3y

When Yahweh says that people will know that he is Yahweh, he is implying that they will know that he is the one true God who has supreme authority and power. Alternate translation: “understand that I am Yahweh, the one true God” or “realize that I, Yahweh, have supreme power and authority” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 35:5
## ix3r
Possible meanings of this metaphor are (1) “you gave them over to their enemies who killed them with swords” or (2) “you killed them with swords.” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## mv7g
“at a time of disaster”

# 35:6
## ax82
Here “bloodshed” is a metonym for killing. Alternate translation: “I will make it easy for your enemies to kill many of you” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## rj8w
Here “bloodshed” is a metonym for killing. Yahweh speaks of bloodshed as if it were a person who could chase them. Alternate translation: “your enemies will chase you down and kill you” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## sr9i
Here “bloodshed” is a metonym for killing. Alternate translation: “Since you did not hate it when enemies brutally killed the people of Israel” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 35:7
## a6in
See [[EZK-a6in]]
## hhc6
Possible meanings are (1) “cut off” is a metaphor that means to destroy. Alternate translation: “I will destroy anyone who enters it or leaves it” or (2) “cut off” is a metaphor that means to stop someone from doing something. Alternate translation: “I will make it so that people do not travel back and forth through it” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 35:8
## wbp9
Here “sword” represents enemies who fought them in battle. This can be stated in active form. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 31:17](../31/17.md). Alternate translation: “those whom enemies have killed with swords” or “those who have died in battle” (See: [[figs-activepassive]] and [[figs-metonymy]])

# 35:9
## xx8k
“desolate forever.” This may be an exaggeration to emphasize the destruction. (See: [[figs-hyperbole]])

## hy7l
This can be stated in active form. This may be an exaggeration for emphasis. Alternate translation: “People will not live in your cities” (See: [[figs-activepassive]] and [[figs-hyperbole]])

## i7gc
Here “you” is plural. God is speaking to the people of Mount Seir, rather than to a single mountain. (See: [[figs-you]])

# 35:10
## h112
See [[EZK-h112]]
## i7s4
The word “You” refers to the mountain of Seir. Ezekiel is to speak to the mountain as if it can hear him. The message is for the people of Edom. Alternate translation: “Your people said” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## zmt2
“the lands of Israel and Judah”

## cb3b
The word “mine” can be stated in plural form. Alternate translation: “will become ours”

## we2l
The word “we” refers to the people of Edom.

## dw47
It is implied that Yahweh was protecting Israel and Judah. Alternate translation: “but Yahweh was there protecting Israel and Judah” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 35:11
## d51p
Possible meanings are (1) “I will punish you because of your anger and jealousy” or (2) “just as you acted against the people of Israel with anger and jealousy, I will act against you with anger and jealousy.”

# 35:12
## k1s3
See [[EZK-k1s3]]
## y3tw
Here “mountains” represents the whole land of Israel. (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

## wts3
This phrase can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “They are in ruins” (See: [[figs-activepassive]])

## uc8j
The people of Mount Seir taking the land of Israel and using it for themselves is spoken of as if they were wild animals that would devour the mountains of Israel. Alternate translation: “they are here for us to devour” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

# 35:14
## yi17
See [[EZK-yi17]]
## rhr8
This can be stated in first person. Alternate translation: “This is what I, the Lord Yahweh, say” (See: [[figs-123person]])

## w5h5
Here “you” refers to Mount Seir, but the message is for the people of Edom. The abstract noun “desolation” can be stated as an adjective. Alternate translation: “Because of what your people did I will make you desolate” (See: [[figs-personification]] and [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## bfc7
Here “earth” represents the people of the earth. The word “entire” is a generalization that refers only to people near Mount Seir. Alternate translation: “people who know that I have destroyed you rejoice” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 35:15
## zg6c
This speaks of the land that Yahweh gave to the Israelites as their inheritance. Alternate translation: “As you rejoiced when I made the land of the Israelites desolate” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## et5r
Possible meanings are (1) I will make your land desolate” or (2) “I will rejoice when your land is desolate” or (3) “I will make other people rejoice because of your desolation.”

## d1la
The word “they” possibly refers to (1) “the people of the earth” or (2) “the people of Israel and Judah.”

## zh9m

God wants Ezekiel to speak to the mountains as if they were people. The message is for the people of Israel. (See: [[figs-personification]])

# 36:2
## k2eq
This is an expression of joy. It can be translated as “I am very happy” or “This is great.”

“The very old mountains.” This refers to the high mountains of Israel.

# 36:3

## iz4b
“because you were attacked from every direction” or “because your enemies attacked you from every direction”

## x8k1

## d53g

# 36:5
## wpy5
This speaks of Yahweh’s fury as if it were a fire. Yahweh loves Israel very much, so he becomes jealous and angry when other nations mock it. Alternate translation: “because of my intense jealousy” or “because of my very strong anger” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## s5ej
“and against all of Edom”

## suz3
Here “heart” and “spirit” represent a person’s inner being. The ideas of having joy and disdain can be expressed with the verbs “rejoiced” and “despised.” Alternate translation: “who despised the people of Israel and rejoiced while they took my land” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

# 36:6
## i6q1
The word “Behold” here adds emphasis to what follows. Alternate translation: “Indeed!”

## tf39
The words “fury” and “anger” mean basically the same thing. Together they emphasize the intensity of his anger. Alternate translation: “Because I am extremely angry” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## ia8c
“other nations have insulted you” or “other nations have mocked you”

The people experiencing shame are spoken of as if they will carry their shame. Alternate translation: “that people will certainly mock the nations that surround you” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

The word “you” refers to the mountains of Israel.

## cn2k

## fp47

## w5ba
Yahweh forgiving the people and causing them to no longer sin is spoken of as if he would cleanse them with water. The phrase “you will be purified” can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “I will purify you as if I were sprinkling you with pure water, and I will cause you to stop worshiping idols” (See: [[figs-metaphor]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

“all the things that made you unclean”

## sqa4
See [[EZK-sqa4]]
## d81b
Yahweh causing the people to no longer be stubborn but to love and serve Yahweh is spoken of as if he will take away their old heart and give them a new heart and spirit. (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## hzb2
Here “heart” and “spirit” represent a person’s thoughts, attitudes, and emotions. See how you translated “heart” and “spirit” in [Ezekiel 11:19](../11/19.md).

“within you” or “inside of you”

## u62l

## xjw7
“I will call the grain to come.” This phrase presents the grain as a servant of Yahweh. Alternate translation: “I will cause there to be grain in the land of Israel” (See: [[figs-personification]])

## b8fw
Yahweh causing a famine in the land is spoken of as if he put famine on the people. Alternate translation: “I will no longer cause there to be a famine” or “I will no longer cause there to be no food” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 36:30
## a3wr
Experiencing shame is spoken of as if the people had to carry the shame. Alternate translation: “the nations will no longer make you feel ashamed because you suffer from famine” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

The words “ashamed” and “disgraced” share similar meanings. Together they emphasize the intensity of the shame. Alternate translation: “So be very ashamed” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## pqu1
The word “hand” is often used to refer to someone’s power or action. A person with his hand on another person has power over that other person. See how you translated a similar phrase in [Ezekiel 1:3](../01/03.md). Alternate translation: “Yahweh was controlling me” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## j93q
“in the middle”

# 37:2
## g6gr
“in every direction”

## u57b
The word “Behold” here alerts us to pay attention to the surprising information that follows.

# 37:3
## h9dr
“Son of a human being” or “Son of humanity.” God calls Ezekiel this to emphasize that Ezekiel is only a human being. God is eternal and powerful, but humans are not. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 2:1](../02/01.md). Alternate translation: “Mortal person” or “Human”

## i1nm

## ns2x
The noun “breath” can be stated as the verb “breathe.” Alternate translation: “I will cause you to breathe”

## xr2z
The Hebrew word translated as “breath” in these verses is translated as “spirit” by a few modern versions. It is also translated as “wind” in [Ezekiel 37:9](../37/09.md).

# 37:6
## z7hm
the tissue that connects muscles to bones

## q7zv
When Yahweh says that people will know that he is Yahweh, he is implying that they will know that he is the one true God who has supreme authority and power. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 6:7](../06/07.md). Alternate translation: “understand that I am Yahweh, the one true God” or “realize that I, Yahweh, have supreme power and authority” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

This refers to the parts of human bodies that are like hard strings and hold the bones and muscles together. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 37:6](../37/06.md).

## g4u1

The word “Behold” here adds emphasis to what follows. Alternate translation: “Indeed!”

# 38:intro

# 38:1
## y6kr
This is an idiom that is used to introduce something that God told his prophets or his people. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 3:16](../03/16.md). Alternate translation: “Yahweh spoke this message” or “Yahweh spoke these words” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 38:2
## er1m
This is a command to stare at Gog and Magog as a symbol of punishing the people there. See how you translated a similar phrase in [Ezekiel 4:3](../04/03.md). Alternate translation: “Stare at the land of Magog and at Gog, the chief prince … Tubal” or “Stare at Gog, the chief prince … Tubal, and at the land of Magog so that they will be harmed” (See: [[translate-symaction]])

## f2v4
Here “face” is a metonym for attention or gaze, and “set your face” represents staring. Alternate translation: “stare” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## ugx2
It is implied that Magog is the land over which Gog rules. Alternate translation: “Gog who rules over the land of Magog” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## e6y7
This is the name of a leader or king who ruled in the land of Magog. (See: [[translate-names]])

## v7t6
This is the name of an ancient nation that was probably located in the land that is now Turkey. Magog might be the ancient nation of Lydia.

## sz93
This expression occurs twice in these verses. Some modern versions, however, interpret the Hebrew expression as “the chief of Rosh, Meshech, and Tubal.” This is another title for Gog. Alternate translation: “who is the chief prince of Meshech and Tubal” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

## r1k4
See how you translated these names in [Ezekiel 32:26](../32/26.md).

## aqh7
This emphasizes the importance of the statement that follows. It can be translated as “Look!” or “Listen!” or “Pay attention to what I am about to tell you!”

Possible meanings are (1) Yahweh will send literal fire down on Gog and his army or (2) “fire” is a metonym for the destruction that it causes. (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## f28e
This is the name of an ancient nation that probably lived in the land that is now Turkey. Magog might be the ancient nation of Lydia. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 38:2](../38/02.md).

## me83
When Yahweh says that people will know that he is Yahweh, he is implying that they will know that he is the one true God who has supreme authority and power. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 6:7](../06/07.md). Alternate translation: “understand that I am Yahweh, the one true God” or “realize that I, Yahweh, have supreme power and authority” (See: [[figs-explicit]])

# 39:7
## y4tq
See [[EZK-y4tq]]
## j1lr
Here the metonym “my holy name” refers to Yahweh’s character. This can be stated in active form. Alternate translation: “I will make my people, Israel, know that I am holy” (See: [[figs-metonymy]] and [[figs-activepassive]])

# 39:8
## y96a
This tells the reader to pay special attention to what follows. Alternate translation: “Look!” or “Listen!” or “Pay attention to what I am about to tell you!”

## k6bb
These two phrases have similar meaning and emphasize the fact that this will really happen. Alternate translation: “is surely going to happen” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

# 39:9
## lw4x
See [[EZK-lw4x]]
## t6ss
These two phrases mean the same thing. The Israelites will use the wood from the weapons as kindling for fires. Alternate translation: “to start fires” (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## jr6e
This list includes all the typical weapons of war of that day. It may represent weapons in general.

## k28p
wooden sticks used as a weapon

# 39:10
## f3tl
Here “to take” and “to plunder” mean the same thing. Gog intended to take Israel’s possessions, but Yahweh prevented him so that he was not able to do that. (See: [[figs-doublet]])

## l3cu
Translate “plunder” as in [Ezekiel 23:46](../23/46.md).

## v4w4
“son of a human being” or “son of humanity.” God calls Ezekiel this to emphasize that Ezekiel is only a human being. God is eternal and powerful, but humans are not. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 2:1](../02/01.md). Alternate translation: “mortal person” or “human”

## fx3j
“to the feast” or “to the slaughter.” Yahweh means that he will give the birds and animals a very good meal and not that he is worshiping them.

# 39:18
## fiv2

the temple

## mj6n

## j1kj

## icf3
about 2 meters

# 41:6
## m9sv
“three stories”

## p4m5
“The house had ledges all around for the side rooms all around.” This way the side rooms could rest on the ledge of the wall.

## sy7s
“so that the ledges could support”

## u4ci
“for there were no supports in the wall of the house.” The people who built the temple did not want stones or wood that would support the side rooms to be sticking out from the wall of the sanctuary.

# 41:20
## cf7z
“the temple”

# 41:22
## fh5t
These words are the end of the sentence that begins with the words “Their appearance was like the appearance of” in verse 21. Possible meanings of the sentence are (1) as it is translated in the ULT or (2) “The appearance of one was like the appearance of the other. The wooden altar in front of the holy place was.” The abstract noun “appearance” can be translated as a verb. Alternate translation: “They appeared the same way the wooden altar in front of the holy place appeared. They were” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## lqs8
Each long cubit was about 54 centimeters. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 40:5](../40/05.md). Alternate translation: “about 1.6 meters … about 1.1 meters” (See: [[translate-bdistance]])

# 41:23
## wx5m

# 41:24
## p6xg

## eq5j
“both of the doors for both the holy place and the most holy place had two parts”

# 43:intro
## n8nq
See [[EZK-n8nq]]
# 43:2
## qi98
The word “Behold” here alerts the reader to pay attention to the surprising information that follows.

## e4w7
This simply means “a lot of water.” It could refer to a loud river or a large waterfall or the waves crashing at the ocean. All of these are very loud. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 1:24](../01/24.md).

## m5fd
“the earth was full of bright light from his glory”

# 43:3
## k5tf
“The glory of God coming from the east was”

## bi4l
Possible meanings are (1) the second phrase beginning with “according to” explains the meaning of the first phrase beginning with “according to.” Alternate translation: “It was according to the appearance of the vision that I saw when he had come to destroy the city” or (2) the first phrase refers to the vision that Ezekiel had just seen of God’s glory. Alternate translation: “The appearance of this vision that I saw was according to the vision that I saw when he had come to destroy the city”

## s248
The abstract noun “appearance” can be translated as a verb. Alternate translation: “just like what appeared in the vision” (See: [[figs-abstractnouns]])

## f83h
“like the vision”

## akc5
“when the God of Israel had come to destroy the city.” If the earlier Hebrew reading “when I had come to destroy the city” is used, then “destroy the city” is a synecdoche for “prophesy that the city will be destroyed.” Alternate translation: “when I had come to prophesy that the city will be destroyed” or “when I had come to prophesy that the God of Israel will destroy the city” (See: [[figs-synecdoche]])

# 43:5
## r649
Your language may have a different word to show that Ezekiel was surprised by what he saw.

# 43:7
## p4vj
The idols that the people’s kings worshiped are spoken of as if they are corpses because the idols are not alive. Alternate translation: “the lifeless idols that their kings worshiped” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

# 43:8
## z6lz
“The Israelites profaned”

## lyg4
“the disgusting things they did.” God was angry because the people were worshiping idols and false gods. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 5:9](../05/09.md).

## c7nz
The phrase “consumed” here means “completely destroyed.” Alternate translation: “completely destroyed them because I was angry” (See: [[figs-idiom]])

# 43:9
## mkm1
The idols that the people’s kings worshiped are spoken of as if they are corpses because the idols are not alive. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 43:7](../43/07.md). Alternate translation: “the lifeless idols that their kings worshiped” (See: [[figs-metaphor]])

## gg2b

## e5qp

## i8xe
“will keep its pattern”

## rn66
“the instruction” or “the rule”

## pq2x

## n333
“absolutely holy”

## yaf4
“This is important!” Your language may have a way of indicating that the words that follow are important.

# 43:18
## t97x
“Yahweh said”

## g966
“Son of a human being” or “Son of humanity.” God calls Ezekiel this to emphasize that Ezekiel is only a human being. God is eternal and powerful, but humans are not. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 2:1](../02/01.md). Alternate translation: “Mortal person” or “Human”

## e9g4
“the rules” or “the instructions”

# 43:19
## kl54
The word “you” is singular. (See: [[figs-you]])

## q7f2
Yahweh speaks of himself by name to express the certainty of what he is declaring. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 5:11](../05/11.md). Alternate translation: “this is what the Lord Yahweh has declared” or “this is what I, the Lord Yahweh, have declared” (See: [[figs-123person]])

# 43:20
## w2ku
The word “you” is singular. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 43:19](../43/19.md). (See: [[figs-you]])

## d2gh
The horns were the parts of the altar at the four corners of the altar that stuck up above the rest of the altar. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 43:15](../43/15.md).

# 43:22
## wq8s
The word “you” and the command refer to Ezekiel and so are singular. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 43:19](../43/19.md). (See: [[figs-pronouns]] and [[figs-you]])

# 43:23
## du6v
All instances of “you” and the commands refer to Ezekiel and so are singular. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 43:19](../43/19.md). (See: [[figs-pronouns]] and [[figs-you]])

# 43:24
## i436
The altar on which they will sacrifice the bull and ram is in front of the temple, where the presence of Yahweh dwells.

# 43:25
## kse4
This is spoken to Ezekiel and so the word “You” is singular. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 43:19](../43/19.md). (See: [[figs-pronouns]] and [[figs-you]])

# 43:27
## w2ig
This phrase is used here to mark an important part of the instructions. If your language has a way for doing this, you could consider using it here.

## c3ch
The words “your” and “you” are second person plural and refer to the people of Israel in general. (See: [[figs-pronouns]] and [[figs-you]])

## sbu8

## nq7p

## kvb9
The word “house” is a metonym for the family that lives in the house, in this case the Israelites, the descendants of Jacob over many years. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 3:1](../03/01.md). Alternate translation: “the Israelites” or “the Israelite people group” (See: [[figs-metonymy]])

## kwy1
This is the first month of the Hebrew calendar. The first day is near the end of March on Western calendars. (See: [[translate-hebrewmonths]] and [[translate-ordinal]])

## zx5a
The word “you” is singular and refers to whoever is the prince in Israel. (See: [[figs-you]])

## p6gu
“Son of a human being” or “Son of humanity.” God calls Ezekiel this to emphasize that Ezekiel is only a human being. God is eternal and powerful, but humans are not. See how you translated this in [Ezekiel 2:1](../02/01.md). Alternate translation: “Mortal person” or “Human”

## eh61
